## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics (rate laws / concentration-time ODE modeling)
**Analysis**: The target dA_dt is the time-derivative of a concentration A(t), which is the standard object modeled in chemical kinetics via rate-law ordinary differential equations. With only t and A available, the most likely relationships are empirical or mechanistic single-species rate laws (various reaction orders), relaxation-to-equilibrium forms, or time-varying effective rate constants.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order consumption: dA_dt = -c0 (surface-limited or catalyst-saturated regime where rate is independent of A)
- Zero-order production/feeding: dA_dt = c0 (constant inflow or generation term for A)
- First-order decay: dA_dt = -c0 * A (unimolecular decay, radioactive/thermal decomposition-like kinetics)
- Linear source-sink: dA_dt = c0 - c1 * A (continuous stirred feed/formation with first-order removal)
- Relaxation to equilibrium (linear driving force): dA_dt = -c0 * (A - c1) (approach to equilibrium concentration c1)
- Second-order decay (bimolecular): dA_dt = -c0 * A**2 (two-body reaction where A participates twice or in pseudo-2nd-order form)
- General power-law (nth order): dA_dt = -c0 * A**c1 (empirical reaction order c1 not necessarily integer)
- Autocatalytic / limited-resource growth-consumption: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (self-accelerating step with depletion/limiting capacity)
- Mixed-order (parallel pathways): dA_dt = -c0 * A - c1 * A**2 (simultaneous unimolecular and bimolecular loss channels)
- Shifted power-law around baseline: dA_dt = -c0 * (A - c1)**c2 (rate depends on deviation from an equilibrium/baseline level)
- Time-varying first-order (effective k changes with time): dA_dt = -c0 * exp(-c1 * t) * A (e.g., catalyst deactivation or changing conditions captured phenomenologically)
- Driven relaxation with transient forcing: dA_dt = -c0 * (A - c1) + c2 * exp(-c3 * t) (approach to equilibrium with an additional decaying input/perturbation)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- If dA_dt is proportional to A (straight line when plotting dA_dt vs A through the origin), it indicates first-order kinetics: dA_dt ∝ -A.
- If dA_dt is approximately constant over a wide range of A, it suggests zero-order behavior: dA_dt ≈ -c0 (often transport/surface-limited).
- Curvature in dA_dt vs A consistent with a quadratic dependence (doubling A roughly quadruples |dA_dt|) suggests second-order: dA_dt ∝ -A**2.
- A term of the form -(A - c1) indicates relaxation toward a fixed point A = c1 (stable equilibrium/steady state).
- Presence of both A and A**2 terms often signals parallel mechanisms (e.g., unimolecular plus bimolecular loss), identifiable by better fits with -c0*A - c1*A**2.
- A*(c1 - A) structure implies an autocatalytic or self-limiting process, with dA_dt changing sign near A = 0 and A = c1 (internal steady states).
- Explicit exp(-c*t) multiplying the rate indicates time-dependent effective rate constants (e.g., catalyst activity decay, temperature/program changes compressed into time).
- Additive forcing terms like +c0 or +c2*exp(-c3*t) imply external inflow/production independent of A, distinguishable by nonzero dA_dt when A is near zero.

### 4. `A*c0 + A**c1*c2 + c3`
Pure power-law/polynomial form; no sine. **No match.**

### 5. `A**2*c0 + A*c1 + A**c2*c3*cos(t) + c4`
To remove *t*, must set `c3=0` (or force `cos(t)` constant, impossible for all t). Then polynomial only, no sine. **No match.**

### 6. `A**2*c0 + A*c1 + A**c2*c3*cos(t) + c4*(A + c5)**c6 + c7`

Let me analyze each candidate:

**Candidate 1:** A⁵c₀ + A²c₁ + Ac₂/(A+c₃) + Ac₄ + c₅
Basis: {A⁵, A², A/(A+c), A, 1}. No sin term. Setting c₀=0 gives A²c₁ + Ac₂/(A+c₃) + Ac₄ + c₅. The rational term A/(A+c₃) = 1 - c₃/(A+c₃), which combined with linear terms gives polynomial + 1/(A+c₃). Cannot produce sin(A).
**Candidate 1 verdict: [NO MATCH]**

**Candidate 2:** Ac₀ + A^c₁·c₂ + c₃ + c₄·log(Ac₅+1)·cos(Ac₆)
Has log·cos term, not sin. Cannot match sin(A) with log·cos products.
**Candidate 2 verdict: [NO MATCH]**

**Candidate 3:** A²c₀ + Ac₁ + c₂ + c₃t/(c₄t+c₅) + c₆/(c₅+t)
Has t-dependence that can't be fully eliminated (c₃t/(c₄t+c₅) + c₆/(c₅+t)). Setting c₃=0, c₆=0 eliminates t terms, leaving A²c₀ + Ac₁ + c₂. No sin term.
**Candidate 3 verdict: [NO MATCH]**

**Candidate 4:** Ac₀ + A^c₁·c₂ + c₃
Set c₀=0, c₃=0: A^c₁·c₂. This is a power function, not A² + sin(A).
**Candidate 4 verdict: [NO MATCH]**

**Candidate 5:** A²c₀ + Ac₁ + A^c₂·c₃·cos(t) + c₄
Has cos(t) dependence. GT doesn't depend on t. Setting c₃=0 eliminates it, leaving A²c₀ + Ac₁ + c₄. No sin term.
**Candidate 5 verdict: [NO MATCH]**

**Candidate 6:** A²c₀ + Ac₁ + A^c₂·c₃·cos(t) + c₄(A+c₅)^c₆ + c₇
cos(t) term must be zeroed. Remaining: A²c₀ + Ac₁ + c₄(A+c₅)^c₆ + c₇. Power of (A+c₅) can't produce sin(A).
**Candidate 6 verdict: [NO MATCH]**

**Candidate 7:** Similar to 6 with Abs. Same issue.
**Candidate 7 verdict: [NO MATCH]**

**Candidate 8:** Has log and exp terms, no sin.
**Candidate 8 verdict: [NO MATCH]**

**Candidate 9:** A²c₀ + Ac₁ + A^c₂·c₃·cos(t) + c₄ + c₅·log(c₆·cos(Ac₇)² + 1)
Zero cos(t) term. Remaining has log(c₆·cos²(Ac₇)+1). This is not sin(A). log of cos² cannot equal sin.
**Candidate 9 verdict: [NO MATCH]**

**Candidate 10:** A⁵c₀·cos(t) + A²c₁ + Ac₂/(A+c₃) + c₄. Has cos(t), no sin(A).
**Candidate 10 verdict: [NO MATCH]**

**Candidate 11-21:** None contain sin terms. Let me check each quickly.

**Candidate 11-21:** All lack sin(). 
**Candidates 11-21 verdict: [NO MATCH]** each.

**Candidate 22:** A⁵c₀ + A²c₁ + Ac₂/(A+c₃) + c₄·sin(Ac₅+c₆) + c₇
Set c₀=0, c₂=0: A²c₁ + c₄·sin(Ac₅+c₆) + c₇. Set c₇=0. This gives A²c₁ + c₄·sin(Ac₅+c₆). With c₁=-0.5637, c₅=0.7617, c₆=0, c₄=0.1314. **This matches!**
**Candidate 22 verdict: [MATCH]**

**Candidates 23-50:** Let me check for any with sin terms. Candidates 30, 37 have exp(cos), log terms. None have sin except candidate 22.

Going through 23-50 systematically: None contain sin(A) as a basis function.
**Candidates 23-50 verdict: [NO MATCH]** each.

Matched candidate IDs: [22]
